<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Partition_of_Ireland" title="Partition of Ireland">Partition of Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a></div>
<p>In 1921, with the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a>, six counties in the northeast remained in the United Kingdom as <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a>. It is predominately religion, historical, and political differences that divide the two communities of (<a href="/wiki/Irish_nationalism" title="Irish nationalism">nationalism</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unionists_(Ireland)" title="Unionists (Ireland)">unionism</a>). Four polls taken between 1989 and 1994 revealed that when asked to state their national identity, over 79% of Northern Irish Protestants replied "British" or "Ulster" with 3% or less replying "Irish", while over 60% of Northern Irish Catholics replied "Irish" with 13% or less replying "British" or "Ulster".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> A survey in 1999 showed that 72% of Northern Irish Protestants considered themselves "British" and 2% "Irish", with 68% of Northern Irish Catholics considering themselves "Irish" and 9% "British".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> The survey also revealed that 78% of Protestants and 48% of all respondents felt "Strongly British", while 77% of Catholics and 35% of all respondents felt "Strongly Irish". 51% of Protestants and 33% of all respondents felt "Not at all Irish", while 62% of Catholics and 28% of all respondents felt "Not at all British".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Surnames in the nine-county Province of <a href="/wiki/Ulster" title="Ulster">Ulster</a> tend to differ based on which community families originate from. Ulster Protestants tend to have either English or <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scottish</a> surnames while Catholics tend to have Irish surnames, although this is not always the case.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> There are many Catholics in nine-county Ulster with surnames such as Adams, Emerson, Whitson, Livingstone, Hardy, Tennyson, Galbraith, McCausland, MacDonald (this surname is also common with Highland Roman Catholics in Scotland), Dunbar, Groves, Legge, Scott, Gray, Page, Stewart, Roberts, Rowntree, Henderson, et al., due to intermarriage.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Recent history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland" title="Demographics of the Republic of Ireland">Demographics of the Republic of Ireland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Demography of Northern Ireland">Demography of Northern Ireland</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religions_in_Ireland">Religions in Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Religions in Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the Republic of Ireland, as of 2011, 3,861,335 people or about 84.16% of the population claim to be Roman Catholic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> about 41.6% of the population are Protestant (19.1% Presbyterian, 13.7% Church of Ireland, 3.0% Methodist, 5.8% Other Christian) whilst approximately 40.8% are Catholic as of 2011.</p>
<p>The 31st <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Eucharistic_Congress" title="International Eucharistic Congress">International Eucharistic Congress</a> was held in <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> in 1932, that year being the supposed 1,500th anniversary of Saint Patrick's arrival. Ireland was then home to 3,171,697 Catholics, about a third of whom attended the Congress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time1932_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Time1932-73">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> It was noted in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Time_Magazine" title="Time Magazine">Time Magazine</a></i> that the Congress' special theme would be "the Faith of the Irish."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time1932_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-Time1932-73">[73]</a></sup> The massive crowds were repeated at Pope <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Paul_II" title="John Paul II">John Paul II</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II%27s_visit_to_Ireland" title="Pope John Paul II's visit to Ireland">Mass in Phoenix Park</a> in 1979.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> The idea of faith has affected the question of Irish identity even in relatively recent times, apparently more so for Catholics and Irish-Americans:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>What defines an Irishman? His faith, his place of birth? What of the Irish-Americans? Are they Irish? Who is more Irish, a Catholic Irishman such as <a href="/wiki/James_Joyce" title="James Joyce">James Joyce</a> who is trying to escape from his Catholicism and from his Irishness, or a Protestant Irishman like <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Wilde" title="Oscar Wilde">Oscar Wilde</a> who is eventually becoming Catholic? Who is more Irish... someone like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C.S._Lewis" title="C.S. Lewis">C.S. Lewis</a>, an Ulster Protestant, who is walking towards it, even though he never ultimately crosses the threshold?<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>This has been a matter of concern over the last century for the followers of nationalist ideologists such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DP_Moran" title="DP Moran">DP Moran</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Irish_identity">Irish identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Irish identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Thomas_Davis_(Young_Irelander)" title="Thomas Davis (Young Irelander)">Thomas Davis</a>, a prominent <a href="/wiki/Protestant_Irish_nationalists" title="Protestant Irish nationalists">Protestant Irish nationalist</a> who founded the <a href="/wiki/Young_Ireland" title="Young Ireland">Young Ireland</a> movement, identified the Irish as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celtic_nation" title="Celtic nation">Celtic nation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-davis_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-davis-77">[77]</a></sup> He estimated that ethnically, 5/6ths of the nation were either of Gaelic Irish-origin, descended from returned Scottish Gaels (including much of the <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Ulster_Scots" title="Ulster Scots">Ulster Scots</a>) and some Celtic Welsh (such as his own ancestors and those carrying surnames such as Walsh and Griffiths).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-davis_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-davis-77">[77]</a></sup> As part of this he was a staunch supporter of the <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish language</a> as the "national language".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-davis_77-2"><a href="#cite_note-davis-77">[77]</a></sup> In regards to the Germanic minority in Ireland (of Norman and Anglo-Saxon origin) he believed that they could be assimilated into Irishness if they had a "willingness to be part of the Irish Nation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ireland joined the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Community" title="European Community">European Community</a> in 1973, and Irish citizens became additionally <a href="/wiki/Citizenship_of_the_European_Union" title="Citizenship of the European Union">Citizens of the European Union</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a> signed in 1992. This brought a further question for the future of Irish identity; whether Ireland was "closer to <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a> than to <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>:"</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>History and geography have placed Ireland in a very special location between America and Europe... As Irish people our relationships with the United States and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> are complex. Geographically we are closer to Berlin than Boston. Spiritually we are probably a lot closer to Boston than Berlin. – <a href="/wiki/Mary_Harney" title="Mary Harney">Mary Harney</a>, <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A1naiste" title="Tánaiste">Tánaiste</a>, 2000<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Irish_diaspora">Irish diaspora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Irish_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Irish diaspora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Irish_diaspora" title="Irish diaspora">Irish diaspora</a></div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">Irish American</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irish_Argentine" title="Irish Argentine">Irish Argentine</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_Chilean" title="Irish Chilean">Irish Chilean</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_Australian" title="Irish Australian">Irish Australian</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_Brazilian" title="Irish Brazilian">Irish Brazilian</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_Canadian" title="Irish Canadian">Irish Canadian</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_Mexicans" title="Irish Mexicans">Irish Mexicans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irish_people_in_Jamaica" title="Irish people in Jamaica">Irish people in Jamaica</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_community_in_Britain" title="Irish community in Britain">Irish community in Britain</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scots-Irish_American" title="Scots-Irish American">Scots-Irish American</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">Montserrat</a></div>

<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Leopoldo_ODonnell.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Leopoldo_O%27Donnell,_1st_Duke_of_Tetuan" title="Leopoldo O'Donnell, 1st Duke of Tetuan">Leopoldo O'Donnell, 1st Duke of Tetuan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grandee_of_Spain" title="Grandee of Spain">Grandee of Spain</a> and as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/President_of_the_Government_of_Spain" title="President of the Government of Spain">president of the Government of Spain</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Irish diaspora consists of Irish <a href="/wiki/Emigration" title="Emigration">emigrants</a> and their descendants in <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">countries</a> such as the United States, Great Britain, Canada, Australia, New Zealand, South Africa, and nations of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>. These countries, known sometimes as the <a href="/wiki/Anglosphere" title="Anglosphere">Anglosphere</a>, all have large minorities of Irish descent, who in addition form the core of the Catholic Church in those countries.</p>
<p>Many Irish people were also transported to the island of <a href="/wiki/Montserrat" title="Montserrat">Montserrat</a>, to work as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indentured_servants" title="Indentured servants">indentured servants</a> or exiled prisoners. Unlike <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Africa" title="Ethnic groups of Africa">African</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chattel_slaves" title="Chattel slaves">chattel slaves</a>, the overwhelming majority of Irish laborers who were sent to Montserrat did so by personal choice, and agreed to indentured labor contracts with full and informed knowledge of what that entailed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Some were exiled by the English <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Cromwell" title="Oliver Cromwell">Oliver Cromwell</a> due to the large Irish population and their attempted rebellion on 17 March 1768. To this day, the Island celebrates <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Patrick%27s_Day" title="St. Patrick's Day">St. Patrick's Day</a> as a public holiday to commemorate the event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> People of Irish descent also feature strongly in Latin America, especially in <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> and important minorities in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, Chile, and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>. In 1995, President <a href="/wiki/Mary_Robinson" title="Mary Robinson">Mary Robinson</a> reached out to the "70 million people worldwide who can claim Irish descent."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Today the <a href="/wiki/Diaspora" title="Diaspora">diaspora</a> is believed to contain an estimated 80 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Diaspora_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Diaspora-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PatriceMacMahon.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="456" height="338" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/PatriceMacMahon.jpg/220px-PatriceMacMahon.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/PatriceMacMahon.jpg/330px-PatriceMacMahon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/PatriceMacMahon.jpg/440px-PatriceMacMahon.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PatriceMacMahon.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patrice_de_Mac-Mahon,_Duke_of_Magenta" title="Patrice de Mac-Mahon, Duke of Magenta">Patrice de Mac-Mahon, Duke of Magenta</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marshal_of_France" title="Marshal of France">Marshal of France</a> and as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/President_of_the_French_Republic" title="President of the French Republic">president of the French Republic</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are also large Irish communities in some mainland European countries, notably in Spain, France and Germany. Between 1585 and 1818, over half a million Irish departed Ireland to serve in the wars on the continent, in a constant emigration romantically styled the "<i><a href="/wiki/Flight_of_the_Wild_Geese" title="Flight of the Wild Geese">Flight of the Wild Geese</a></i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WildGeese_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-WildGeese-84">[84]</a></sup> In the early years of the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a>, a French traveller remarked that the Irish "are better soldiers abroad than at home".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Later, Irish brigades in France and Spain fought in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_of_Spanish_Succession" title="War of Spanish Succession">Wars of the Spanish</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_of_Austrian_Succession" title="War of Austrian Succession">Austrian Succession</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WildGeese_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-WildGeese-84">[84]</a></sup> In the words of <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Wellesley,_1st_Duke_of_Wellington" title="Arthur Wellesley, 1st Duke of Wellington">Arthur Wellesley</a>, the Irish-born <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Duke_of_Wellington" title="Duke of Wellington">"Iron Duke" of Wellington</a>, a notable representative of the <a href="/wiki/Irish_military_diaspora" title="Irish military diaspora">Irish military diaspora</a>, "Ireland was an inexhaustible nursery for the finest soldiers".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Legion" title="British Legion">British Legion</a></b> were units that <a href="/wiki/Military_career_of_Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar" title="Military career of Simón Bolívar">fought under Simón Bolívar</a> against Spain for the independence of <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>. Venezuelans called them the <a href="/wiki/Albion" title="Albion">Albion</a> Legion. They were composed of over seven thousand volunteers, mainly <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic War</a> veterans from Great Britain and Ireland. Volunteers in the British Legion were motivated by a combination of both genuine <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political" title="Political">political</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mercenary" title="Mercenary">mercenary</a> motives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MBrown210_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-MBrown210-87">[87]</a></sup> The most famous cause of emigration was the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_Potato_Famine" title="Irish Potato Famine">Great Famine</a> of the late 1840s. A million are thought to have emigrated to <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a> as a result of the famine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> For both the Irish in Ireland and those in the resulting <a href="/wiki/Irish_diaspora" title="Irish diaspora">diaspora</a>, the famine entered <a href="/wiki/Folk_memory" title="Folk memory">folk memory</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> and became a rallying point for various <a href="/wiki/Irish_nationalism" title="Irish nationalism">nationalist movements</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JohnCarrollGilbertStuart.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="921" data-file-width="754" height="269" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/JohnCarrollGilbertStuart.jpg/220px-JohnCarrollGilbertStuart.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/JohnCarrollGilbertStuart.jpg/330px-JohnCarrollGilbertStuart.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/JohnCarrollGilbertStuart.jpg/440px-JohnCarrollGilbertStuart.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JohnCarrollGilbertStuart.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/John_Carroll_(bishop)" title="John Carroll (bishop)">John Carroll</a>, first Roman Catholic bishop and archbishop of the United States</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>People of Irish descent are the second largest self-reported ethnic group in the United States, after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_American" title="German American">German Americans</a>. Nine of the signatories of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Declaration_of_Independence" title="American Declaration of Independence">American Declaration of Independence</a> were of Irish origin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-irishpresidents_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-irishpresidents-90">[90]</a></sup> Among them was the sole Catholic signatory, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Carroll_of_Carrollton" title="Charles Carroll of Carrollton">Charles Carroll of Carrollton</a>, whose family were the descendants of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ely_O%27Carroll" title="Ely O'Carroll">Ely O'Carroll</a>, an Irish prince who had suffered under Cromwell.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> At least twenty-five <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">presidents of the United States</a> have some Irish ancestral origins, including <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-whtaft_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-whtaft-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hardingquest_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-hardingquest-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abouttruman_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-abouttruman-95">[95]</a></sup> Since <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> took office in 1961, every American President (with the exception of Gerald Ford and Donald Trump) has had some Irish blood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DIG_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-DIG-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> An Irish-American, <a href="/wiki/James_Hoban" title="James Hoban">James Hoban</a>, was the designer of the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a>. <a href="/wiki/John_Barry_(naval_officer)" title="John Barry (naval officer)">Commodore John Barry</a>, who was born in <a href="/wiki/County_Wexford" title="County Wexford">County Wexford</a>, was the father of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JFK-John_Barry_Memorial.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="508" data-file-width="760" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/JFK-John_Barry_Memorial.jpg/220px-JFK-John_Barry_Memorial.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/JFK-John_Barry_Memorial.jpg/330px-JFK-John_Barry_Memorial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/JFK-John_Barry_Memorial.jpg/440px-JFK-John_Barry_Memorial.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JFK-John_Barry_Memorial.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> visiting the <a href="/wiki/John_Barry_(naval_officer)" title="John Barry (naval officer)">John Barry</a> Memorial in <a href="/wiki/Wexford" title="Wexford">Wexford</a>, Ireland</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the mid-19th century, large numbers of Irish immigrants were conscripted into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_regiments" title="Irish regiments">Irish regiments</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a> at the time of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican-American_War" title="Mexican-American War">Mexican-American War</a>. The vast majority of the 4,811 Irish-born soldiers served in the U.S. Army, but some defected to the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Army" title="Mexican Army">Mexican Army</a>, primarily to escape mistreatment by Anglo-Protestant officers and the strong anti-Catholic discrimination in America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Connaughton_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Connaughton-100">[100]</a></sup> These were the <i>San Patricios</i>, or <a href="/wiki/Saint_Patrick%27s_Battalion" title="Saint Patrick's Battalion">Saint Patrick's Battalion</a>—a group of Irish led by <a href="/wiki/Galway" title="Galway">Galway</a>-born <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_O%27Riley" title="John O'Riley">John O'Riley</a>, with some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Germany" title="Roman Catholicism in Germany">German</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Scotland" title="Roman Catholicism in Scotland">Scottish</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_the_United_States" title="Roman Catholicism in the United States">American Catholics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Connaughton_100-1"><a href="#cite_note-Connaughton-100">[100]</a></sup> They fought until their surrender at the decisive <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Churubusco" title="Battle of Churubusco">Battle of Churubusco</a>, and were executed outside <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> by the American government on 13 September 1847.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Connaughton_100-2"><a href="#cite_note-Connaughton-100">[100]</a></sup> The battalion is commemorated in Mexico each year on 12 September.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 18th and 19th centuries, 300,000 free emigrants and 45,000 convicts left Ireland to settle in Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Today, Australians of Irish descent are one of the largest self-reported ethnic groups in Australia, after English and Australian. In the 2006 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian_Census" title="Australian Census">Census</a>, 1,803,741 residents identified themselves as having Irish ancestry either alone or in combination with another ancestry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> However this figure does not include Australians with an Irish background who chose to nominate themselves as 'Australian' or other ancestries. The Australian embassy in Dublin states that up to 30 percent of the population claim some degree of Irish ancestry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>It is believed that as many as 30,000 Irish people emigrated to Argentina between the 1830s and the 1890s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Argentina_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-Argentina-8">[8]</a></sup> This was encouraged by the clergy, as they considered a Catholic country, Argentina, preferable to a Protestant United States. This flow of emigrants dropped sharply when assisted passage to Australia was introduced at which point the Argentine government responded with their own scheme and wrote to Irish bishops, seeking their support. However, there was little or no planning for the arrival of a large number of immigrants, no housing, no food.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> Many died, others made their way to the United States and other destinations, some returned to Ireland, a few remained and prospered. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Croke" title="Thomas Croke">Thomas Croke</a> Archbishop of Cashel, said: "I most solemnly conjure my poorer countrymen, as they value their happiness hereafter, never to set foot on the Argentine Republic however tempted to do so they may be by offers of a passage or an assurance of comfortable homes."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Some famous Argentines of Irish descent include <a href="/wiki/Che_Guevara" title="Che Guevara">Che Guevara</a>, former president <a href="/wiki/Edelmiro_Juli%C3%A1n_Farrell" title="Edelmiro Julián Farrell">Edelmiro Julián Farrell</a>, and admiral <a href="/wiki/William_Brown_(admiral)" title="William Brown (admiral)">William Brown</a>. There are people of Irish descent all over South America, such as the Chilean liberator <a href="/wiki/Bernardo_O%27Higgins" title="Bernardo O'Higgins">Bernardo O'Higgins</a> and the Peruvian photographer <a href="/wiki/Mario_Testino" title="Mario Testino">Mario Testino</a>. Although some Irish retained their surnames intact, others were assimilated into the Spanish vernacular. The last name <i>O'Brien</i>, for example, became <i>Obregón</i>.</p>
<p>People of Irish descent are also one of the largest self-reported ethnic groups in Canada, after <a href="/wiki/English_Canadian" title="English Canadian">English</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Canadian" title="French Canadian">French</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scottish_Canadian" title="Scottish Canadian">Scottish Canadians</a>. As of 2006, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_Canadian" title="Irish Canadian">Irish Canadians</a> number around 4,354,155.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CanadaCensus_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-CanadaCensus-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
